The Mawla Hadith as Proof of Ali's Authority
Razi uses the famous 'mawla' hadith to argue Ali's authority and superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi interprets the 'Mawla' hadith to argue for Ali's authority and superiority over all creation.

Core Idea
The 'Mawla' hadith proves Ali's authority just as it proves the Prophet's.

Razi presents the tenth proof, based on the famous hadith 'man kuntu mawlahu fa 'Ali mawlahu'. He argues that the term 'mawla' for the Prophet indicates his role as one served and commander, and by extension, the same applies to Ali, making him the best of creation. This passage is a key argument in the debate over leadership after the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp Razi's argument as a whole.
Notice the logical flow: definition of 'mawla', analogy, conclusion, then supporting narration.
2
Identify the key term
Focus on the word 'mawla'. Understand why Razi insists it means 'master and commander' rather than just 'friend'.
This is the crux of the argument.
3
Trace the analogy
Razi draws an analogy: since 'mawla' for the Prophet means he is served and commander, the same must hold for Ali when the hadith is applied to him.
4
Examine the supporting evidence
Razi cites Umar's congratulatory statement as confirmation that 'mawla' implies authority over all believers until the Day of Resurrection.
This shows that even contemporaries understood the word this way.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
How does this argument establish Ali's superiority? Consider the implications for leadership.
This argument is used in sectarian discussions about the caliphate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة العاشرة : قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم من كنت موله فعلي موله ولفظ المولى في حق محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم لا شك أنه يفيد أنه كان مخدوما للكل، وصاحب الأمر فيهم، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك وجب أن يقال في علي : إنه أيضاً مخدوم ونافذ الحكم فيهم، وهذا يوجب كونه أفضل الخلق والذي يدل على أنه يفيد المعنى الذي ذكرناه ما نقل أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لما ذكر هذا الكلام قال عمر لعلي : "بخ بخ يا علي، أصبحت مولى كل مؤمن ومؤمنة إلى يوم القيامة".
The tenth proof: His statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever I am his mawla, 'Ali is his mawla.' And the word 'mawla' with respect to Muhammad (peace be upon him) undoubtedly indicates that he was served by all and the commander over them. If this is so, then it must be said of 'Ali: that he also is served and his command is executed among them. This necessitates his being the best of creation. And what indicates that it conveys the meaning we mentioned is what was narrated: that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) said these words, 'Umar said to 'Ali: 'Well done, O 'Ali, you have become the mawla of every believing man and woman until the Day of Resurrection.'
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) from the well-known hadith, 'man kuntu mawlahu fa 'Ali mawlahu'. Razi argues that the term 'mawla' for the Prophet undoubtedly means he is the one served (makhdum) and the commander (sahib al-amr) over the community. By analogy, 'Ali must also be makhdum and his command executed, which necessitates his superiority over all creation. To support this interpretation, Razi cites the incident where 'Umar congratulated 'Ali, saying 'You have become the mawla of every believer', confirming that 'mawla' here means authority and leadership.

Key Terms
مولى
مخدوم
صاحب الأمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadith only means friendship or love, not leadership.
Correction: Razi argues that 'mawla' for the Prophet indicates command and service, and the same must apply to Ali, establishing authority.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what does 'mawla' mean in the context of the Prophet?
A) Friend
B) Helper
C) Master and commander
D) Neighbor

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi uses the Mawla hadith to argue that Ali is the commander over all believers, making him the best of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that Ali (as) is the mawla of every believer until the Day of Resurrection, how would your treatment of his teachings and example change starting today?
?
Do you find yourself resisting the idea that Ali holds authority over you? What does that reveal about your attachment to your own opinions versus submission to divine appointment?
?
When you hear Umar's congratulation to Ali, do you feel that you have personally accepted Ali as your mawla, or do you keep it at a historical distance? What concrete action can you take this week to demonstrate your allegiance?

Eleventh Argument: Ali's Position Like Harun
Razi's proof from the hadith of Manzilah for Ali's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the hadith 'You are to me as Harun was to Musa' to argue for Ali's superiority over the entire Muslim community.

Core Idea
The hadith of Manzilah establishes Ali's superiority by analogy with Harun's status.

Razi presents a scriptural proof anchored in a well-known hadith. The comparison between Ali and Harun is not merely about relationship but about rank. This lesson unpacks the logical move from the hadith to the conclusion that Ali is the best of the ummah.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its premise
Carefully read the Arabic text and translation. Notice the key terms 'manzilah' and 'afdaliyya'.
The hadith is widely accepted among Muslims.
2
Understand the logical structure
Identify the two premises: the hadith equates Ali's position to Harun's, and Harun was the best of Musa's nation. The conclusion follows necessarily.
The argument is a simple syllogism.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: What makes this argument effective? Does it depend on accepting the hadith as authentic and the premise about Harun's superiority?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الحادية عشرة : قوله انت مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى» صلى الله عليه وسلم وهارون كان أفضل من كل أمة موسى، فوجب أن يكون علي أفضل من كل أمة محمد .
The eleventh proof: His statement (peace be upon him): 'You are to me as Harun was to Musa.' And Harun was the best of the entire nation of Musa, so it must be that 'Ali is the best of the entire nation of Muhammad.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) based on the hadith 'You are to me as Harun was to Musa'. Razi states the premise that Harun was the best of Musa's entire nation. Therefore, by analogy, 'Ali must be the best of Muhammad's entire nation. The argument assumes that the comparison is absolute and that superiority is established through the parallel.

Key Terms
منزلة
أفضلية
هارون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'You are to me as Harun was to Musa' only refers to prophethood, not to superiority.
Correction: Razi argues that the comparison is absolute and includes superiority, because Harun was the best of Musa's nation, so Ali must be the best of Muhammad's nation.

Checkpoint

A) Ali is like Harun in Prophethood
B) Ali is better than all of Muhammad's nation
C) Ali is the successor
D) Ali is the Prophet's cousin

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Manzilah, when combined with the premise of Harun's superiority, yields a strong argument for Ali's supremacy over the entire ummah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Twelfth Proof: Brotherhood Implies Equality
Razi argues that the Prophet's brotherhood with Ali proves Ali's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the Prophet's act of brotherhood with Ali to argue for Ali's supreme rank.

Core Idea
Brotherhood with the Prophet makes Ali equal in rank to the best of creation.

In this argument, Razi draws on a well-known historical event: the Prophet's establishment of brotherhood among the companions, including taking Ali as his own brother. Razi presents this as evidence for Ali's superiority. The passage also includes Ali's own claims to exclusive titles. Let's examine how Razi constructs this proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Note the key claims made by Razi and by Ali himself.
The Arabic contains a minor textual variant, but the meaning is clear.
2
Identify the proof structure
Razi first mentions the act of brotherhood, then cites Ali's statements, and finally gives the logical inference. Trace this sequence.
3
Evaluate the logic
Consider why brotherhood implies equality in rank. How does that lead to Ali being the best after the Prophet?
Razi's argument relies on the principle that each brother takes the place of the other.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية عشرة : أنه لما آخى بين الصحابة اتخذه أخا لنفسه، أن وروي عليا قال في مواضع كثيرة : " أنا عبد الله وأخو رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يقولها أحد بعدي إلا كذاب، أنا الصديق الأكبر، وأنا الفاروق الأعظم، وأنا الذي يفرق بين الحق والباطل " . وإنما قلنا : إن المؤاخاة تدل على الأفضلية لأن المؤاخاة مظنة المساواة في المنصب، وكون كل واحد منهما قائما مقام الآخر ولما كان محمد أفضل من الكل كان القائم مقامه كذلك.
The twelfth proof: That when he established brotherhood among the companions, he took 'Ali as a brother for himself. And it was narrated that 'Ali said in many places: 'I am the servant of Allah and the brother of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace; none says it after me except a liar. I am the greatest Siddiq, and I am the greatest Faruq, and I am the one who distinguishes between truth and falsehood.' And we only say: The brotherhood indicates superiority because brotherhood is a basis for equality in rank, and each of them takes the place of the other. And since Muhammad is the best of all, the one who takes his place is likewise.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) from the act of brotherhood (mu'akha) between the Prophet and 'Ali. Razi cites 'Ali's own claim that he is the 'brother of the Messenger of Allah' and his titles 'Siddiq al-Akbar' and 'Faruq al-A'zam'. The reasoning is that brotherhood implies equality in rank and that each stands in the place of the other. Since the Prophet is the best of all, 'Ali, as his brother and successor in standing, must also be the best.

Key Terms
مؤاخاة
صديق
فاروق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Brotherhood is just a metaphor and does not imply real equality.
Correction: Razi argues that brotherhood in this context implies equality in rank and standing, making Ali the best after the Prophet.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi say the brotherhood (mu'akha) indicates superiority?
A) Because Ali claimed it
B) Because brotherhood implies equality in rank
C) Because the Prophet chose him
D) Because Ali was older

Key Takeaway
Razi uses the Prophet's brotherhood with Ali to argue that Ali is equal in rank to the Prophet, therefore the best of creation after him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Prophet chose Ali as his brother. What does that say about your own attachments? Do you honor those whom the Prophet honored, even when it challenges your loyalties?
?
Razi's proof demands that you accept Ali as the best after the Prophet. Is your soul willing to submit to this, or does pride or prior teaching hold you back? What will you do about that resistance?

Thirteenth Proof: Hadith of Harqus Proves Ali as Best
Razi presents a hadith that the worst is killed by the best, and the killer was Ali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith about Harqus proves that Ali ibn Abi Talib is the best of creation according to Razi's argument.

Core Idea
The killer of the worst must be the best, and Ali was that killer.

This lesson examines the thirteenth proof in Razi's list: a prophetic hadith identifying the worst person (Harqus) and stating that his killer is the best of creation. History confirms that Ali killed him, establishing Ali's superiority. Let's analyze the text and its logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic text of the hadith and its translation. Note the description of Harqus as the worst and the killer as the best.
2
Identify the logical structure
Notice that the argument links two statements: (1) the worst is killed by the best, (2) Ali killed him. Therefore Ali is the best.
The argument is a simple syllogism.
3
Consider alternative interpretations
Reflect on why Razi uses this hadith as a proof. What assumptions underlie the argument? How might opponents object?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة عشرة : ما روي إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال في حرقوص شر الخلق وهو ذو الثدية : يقتله خير الخلق وفي رواية : يقتله خير هذه الأمة، وكان قاتله علي بن طالب. الحجة الرابعة عشرة : قال النبي لفاطمة : إن الله تعالى اطلع على أهل الدنيا فاختار منهم أباك فاتخذه نبياً، ثم اطلع ثانيا فاختار منهم بعلك».
The thirteenth proof: What was narrated: That the Prophet (peace be upon him) said about Harqus, the worst of creation, who was Dhu al-Thudayya: 'He is killed by the best of creation' and in a narration: 'He is killed by the best of this nation.' And his killer was 'Ali ibn Abi Talib. The fourteenth proof: The Prophet said to Fatima: 'Indeed Allah, exalted, looked at the people of the world and chose from them your father and took him as a prophet, then He looked a second time and chose from them your husband.'
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage contains two separate proofs (hujjat) based on hadith. The thirteenth: The Prophet stated that Harqus (Dhu al-Thudayya), who is described as the worst of creation, will be killed by the best of creation (or the best of this nation). It is known that 'Ali was his killer, so 'Ali is the best. The fourteenth: The Prophet told Fatima that Allah first chose her father (the Prophet) from all people, and then second chose her husband ('Ali), implying 'Ali's special status and superiority.

Key Terms
حرقوص
خير الخلق
ذو الثدية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Someone other than Ali killed Harqus or the hadith does not mention Ali by name.
Correction: Razi's argument relies on the known historical fact that Ali was the killer, and the hadith explicitly says the killer is the best.

Checkpoint
According to the thirteenth proof, who killed Harqus?
A) Abu Bakr
B) Umar
C) Ali
D) Uthman

Key Takeaway
The hadith about Harqus establishes Ali's status as the best of creation because he killed the worst, as foretold by the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Fifteenth and Sixteenth Arguments: Sayyid al-Arab and the Best Heir
Razi cites two hadiths naming Ali as 'Sayyid al-Arab' and the best to leave behind.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two hadiths are used as proofs for Ali's superiority over the Companions.

Core Idea
Two hadiths elevate Ali as 'Sayyid al-Arab' and the best one to leave behind.

In this lesson, Razi presents two additional proofs from hadith literature. The first involves a dialogue with Aisha where the Prophet distinguishes his own universal lordship from Ali's leadership over the Arabs. The second is a direct declaration that Ali is his brother, vizier, and the best successor. These narrations are used to argue for Ali's special status.

Guided Path
1
Read the two hadith proofs carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: each proof is introduced separately.
2
Understand the distinction in the first hadith
The Prophet calls himself 'Sayyid al-'Alamin' and Ali 'Sayyid al-Arab'. This distinction shows Ali's high rank over all Arabs.
3
Analyze the titles in the second hadith
The Prophet calls Ali his brother, vizier, and best one to leave behind. These titles imply responsibility and trust.
4
Reflect on how these proofs support Ali's superiority
Consider why Razi uses these hadiths as evidence for Ali's imamate and superiority. The titles are unique to Ali among the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة عشرة : قالت عائشة انا كنت عند النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذ أقبل علي، فقال: هذا سيد العرب قالت فقلت بأبي أنت وأمي ألست سيد العرب؟ فقال: «إنما أنا سيد العالمين، وهو سيد العرب. الحجة السادسة عشرة: روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «إن أخي ووزيري وخير من أتركه بعدي الذي يقضي ديني وينجز وعدي : علي بن أبي طالب.
The fifteenth proof: 'A'isha said: I was with the Prophet (peace be upon him) when 'Ali approached, so he said: 'This is the sayyid (master) of the Arabs.' She said: I said, 'May my father and mother be sacrificed for you, are you not the sayyid of the Arabs?' He said: 'I am only the sayyid of the worlds, and he is the sayyid of the Arabs.' The sixteenth proof: It was narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed my brother, my vizier, and the best of those I leave behind me, the one who will pay my debts and fulfill my promises, is 'Ali ibn Abi Talib.'
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage presents two further proofs from hadith. Fifteenth: 'A'isha narrates that the Prophet called 'Ali 'Sayyid al-Arab' (master of the Arabs) while distinguishing himself as 'Sayyid al-'Alamin' (master of the worlds). This confers a high title on 'Ali. Sixteenth: The Prophet declares 'Ali as his brother, vizier, and the best of those he leaves behind, who will settle his debts and fulfill his promises. This implies 'Ali's superiority over all others.

Key Terms
سيد العرب
وزير
خير من أترك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'sayyid' only means a noble person without implying superiority.
Correction: Razi uses 'sayyid' as a title of supreme leadership, as seen in the distinction between 'Sayyid al-'Alamin' and 'Sayyid al-Arab'.

Checkpoint
In the fifteenth proof, how did the Prophet distinguish himself from Ali?
A) He said he is the sayyid of the Arabs
B) He said he is the sayyid of the worlds
C) He said Ali is his brother
D) He said Ali is his vizier

Key Takeaway
Two hadiths from the Prophet explicitly confer on Ali the titles 'Sayyid al-Arab' and 'best heir,' used as proofs for his superiority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet specifically designated Ali as 'sayyid al-Arab' and 'the best to leave behind', how does that challenge any previous underestimation of Ali's status in your heart? What will you change about how you view him?
?
The Prophet entrusted Ali with paying his debts and fulfilling his promises. Are there any trusts or responsibilities from Allah or His Messenger that you have been negligent in? What is one step you will take today to become more trustworthy like Ali?
?
You have just read two clear hadiths about Ali's superiority. Is there any bias or sectarian influence in your heart that resists this truth? Commit to one action to learn more about the virtues of the Companions without prejudice.

The Seventeenth Proof: Ali is the Best of Mankind
Razi cites a hadith affirming Ali as the best of mankind.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the textual proof from hadith that Ali is the best of mankind according to Razi.

Core Idea
A hadith declares Ali the best; rejecting it is disbelief.

Razi begins his seventeenth argument by citing a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud. The Prophet's statement is presented as definitive proof that Ali is khayr al-bashar. This lesson examines the hadith and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
Read the Arabic text of the hadith and its translation carefully. Note the wording: 'Ali is the best of mankind; whoever refuses has disbelieved.'
The term 'abā' (refused) is pivotal.
2
Identify the proof structure
Recognize that this is a direct textual proof (dalil naqli). Razi does not analyze the chain or content but presents it as a clear statement.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider the severity: rejecting Ali's superiority is equated with disbelief. Think about how this would be received by other Muslim groups.
This is a strong claim that goes beyond mere preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة عشرة : روى ابن مسعود أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «علي خير البشر، من أبي فقد كفر. الحجة الثامنة عشرة : أن عليا لم يكفر بالله تعالى وأن أبا بكر كان في زمان الجاهلية كافراً، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : إن عليا كان أكثر تقوى من أبي بكر ؛ لأن من كان مؤمنا أبدا لا بد وأن يكون أكثر تقوى ممن كان كافرا ثم صار مؤمنا، والأتقى أفضل، لقوله تعالى : وإِنَّ أَكْرَمَكُمْ عِندَ اللَّهِ أَنْقَلَكُمْ ﴾ [الحجرات : ١٣] .
The seventeenth proof: Ibn Mas'ud narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: ''Ali is the best of mankind; whoever refuses has disbelieved.' The eighteenth proof: That 'Ali never disbelieved in Allah, while Abu Bakr was a disbeliever in the time of Jahiliyya. When this is established, we say: Indeed 'Ali was more pious than Abu Bakr, because whoever is always a believer must be more pious than one who was a disbeliever then became a believer. And the more pious is better, according to His statement: 'Indeed the most noble of you in the sight of Allah is the most pious' (49:13).
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage contains two proofs. Seventeenth: A hadith from Ibn Mas'ud states that 'Ali is the best of mankind (khayr al-bashar), and whoever refuses this statement has disbelieved. Eighteenth: Razi argues that 'Ali never disbelieved, whereas Abu Bakr was a polytheist before Islam. Therefore, 'Ali's constant faith makes him more pious (atqa) than Abu Bakr. Since the Quran declares that the most pious is the most noble, 'Ali is superior. This is a comparative proof against one of the other companions.

Key Terms
خير البشر
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith in the seventeenth proof say about whoever refuses that Ali is the best of mankind?
A) They are mistaken
B) They have disbelieved
C) They are sinful
D) They are ignorant

Key Takeaway
Razi uses a hadith to assert that Ali is the best of mankind and rejection is disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read this hadith, what is your immediate reaction? Do you accept it without question, or do you find yourself resisting? What does that resistance reveal about your own biases? Will you sincerely seek the truth about Ali's status, or will you cling to what you were taught?
?
The hadith warns that refusing this truth is disbelief. Are there any Islamic truths that you find yourself refusing because they don't align with your preferences? How will you respond to this challenge today?
?
Imagine standing before Allah and being asked about your stance on Ali. Would you be able to justify your position with knowledge and sincerity, or would you realize you had followed blind imitation? What step will you take today to ensure your beliefs are founded on truth?

The Eighteenth Proof: Ali's Continuous Faith Makes Him Superior
Razi argues that Ali's uninterrupted faith makes him more pious and therefore better than Abu Bakr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's rational argument that Ali's uninterrupted faith makes him more pious and thus superior to Abu Bakr.

Core Idea
Continuous faith yields greater piety, and piety defines nobility.

The eighteenth argument moves from text to reason. Razi compares Ali's lifelong faith with Abu Bakr's prior disbelief, concluding that Ali's constant belief makes him more pious. He then cites the Quranic verse linking nobility to piety to establish superiority.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the premises: Ali never disbelieved, Abu Bakr was a disbeliever in Jahiliyya.
2
Understand the deduction
Razi deduces that Ali is more pious because continuous faith produces greater piety. Trace the logic: always a believer → more pious.
3
Connect to the Quranic verse
Razi cites Quran 49:13 to establish that greater piety means greater nobility. Understand how this completes the argument for Ali's superiority.
The verse is used as a criterion for ranking.
4
Critically evaluate
Consider the assumption that continuous faith always yields greater piety than a faith after disbelief. Is this necessarily true? Razi presents it as a 'must' (la budda).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة عشرة : روى ابن مسعود أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «علي خير البشر، من أبي فقد كفر. الحجة الثامنة عشرة : أن عليا لم يكفر بالله تعالى وأن أبا بكر كان في زمان الجاهلية كافراً، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : إن عليا كان أكثر تقوى من أبي بكر ؛ لأن من كان مؤمنا أبدا لا بد وأن يكون أكثر تقوى ممن كان كافرا ثم صار مؤمنا، والأتقى أفضل، لقوله تعالى : وإِنَّ أَكْرَمَكُمْ عِندَ اللَّهِ أَنْقَلَكُمْ ﴾ [الحجرات : ١٣] .
The seventeenth proof: Ibn Mas'ud narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: ''Ali is the best of mankind; whoever refuses has disbelieved.' The eighteenth proof: That 'Ali never disbelieved in Allah, while Abu Bakr was a disbeliever in the time of Jahiliyya. When this is established, we say: Indeed 'Ali was more pious than Abu Bakr, because whoever is always a believer must be more pious than one who was a disbeliever then became a believer. And the more pious is better, according to His statement: 'Indeed the most noble of you in the sight of Allah is the most pious' (49:13).
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage contains two proofs. Seventeenth: A hadith from Ibn Mas'ud states that 'Ali is the best of mankind (khayr al-bashar), and whoever refuses this statement has disbelieved. Eighteenth: Razi argues that 'Ali never disbelieved, whereas Abu Bakr was a polytheist before Islam. Therefore, 'Ali's constant faith makes him more pious (atqa) than Abu Bakr. Since the Quran declares that the most pious is the most noble, 'Ali is superior. This is a comparative proof against one of the other companions.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That one's past disbelief does not affect one's level of piety after conversion.
Correction: Razi argues that continuous faith results in greater piety than a faith that came after disbelief.

Razi uses the duration of faith and the Quranic criterion of piety to rank Ali above Abu Bakr.

?
This proof ranks based on continuous belief. Have you ever looked down on someone who converted later in life? How does this argument challenge that attitude? Write down one concrete way you will honor a new Muslim this week as an act of humility before Allah.

The Nineteenth Argument: Ali's Equality with the Prophets
Razi uses a hadith equating Ali's virtues to those of five prophets to prove his superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses a hadith equating Ali's virtues to those of five prophets to argue for his superiority over the Companions.

Core Idea
If Ali is equal to prophets who are best, then Ali is best of the Companions.

In this lesson, we examine the nineteenth argument from Imam Razi's Al-Arba'een. Razi presents a hadith that describes Ali as embodying the virtues of five major prophets. Based on this, he constructs a logical case for Ali's superiority over Abu Bakr and all other Companions. Let's follow the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its implication
Read the Arabic hadith and its translation. Notice how Razi interprets the phrase 'look at' to mean equality in those attributes.
The hadith is narrated by Ahmad and al-Bayhaqi.
2
Understand the logical structure
Razi's argument has three premises and a conclusion. Identify each part: (1) Ali equals these prophets in specific virtues, (2) These prophets are superior to all other Companions, (3) Equality with the superior makes one superior.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that Ali is superior to Abu Bakr and all Companions. Consider potential objections, such as whether 'look at' implies full equality.
This is a key point of debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة عشرة : روى أحمد والبيهقي في فضائل الصحابة قال: «من أراد أن ينظر إلى آدم في فضله، وإلى نوح في تقواه، وإلى إبراهيم في حلمه، وإلى موسى في هيبته، وإلى عيسى في عبادته، فلينظر إلى علي بن أبي طالب». ظاهر هذا الحديث يدل على أن عليا كان مساويًا لهؤلاء الأنبياء في هذه الصفات، ولا شك أن هؤلاء الأنبياء كانوا أفضل من أبي بكر وسائر الصحابة، والمساوي للأفضل أفضل، فوجب أن يكون علي أفضل منهم.
The nineteenth proof: Ahmad and al-Bayhaqi narrated in Fada'il al-Sahaba: 'Whoever wishes to look at Adam in his virtue, Noah in his piety, Abraham in his forbearance, Moses in his awe, and Jesus in his worship, let him look at 'Ali ibn Abi Talib.' The apparent meaning of this hadith indicates that 'Ali was equal to these prophets in these attributes, and there is no doubt that these prophets were better than Abu Bakr and the rest of the Companions, and the one equal to the better is better, so it must be that 'Ali is better than them.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) from a hadith collected by Ahmad and al-Bayhaqi. The hadith states that whoever wants to see the virtue of Adam, piety of Noah, forbearance of Abraham, awe of Moses, and worship of Jesus should look at 'Ali. Razi argues that this implies 'Ali is equal to these prophets in those attributes. Since these prophets are undoubtedly superior to Abu Bakr and all other Companions, and equality with the superior makes one superior, 'Ali must be superior to all Companions, including Abu Bakr.

Key Terms
مساو
فضيلة
تقوى
حلم
هيبة
عبادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the hadith only says 'look at' and does not imply equality.
Correction: Razi argues that the apparent meaning (zahir) of the hadith indicates equality, as the comparison is made specifically in virtues.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, why does the equality of Ali with the prophets make him better than the Companions?
A) Because the prophets are better than the Companions
B) Because Ali is better than the prophets
C) Because the hadith says so
D) Because of Ali's lineage

Key Takeaway
Razi's nineteenth argument uses a hadith to establish Ali's equality with prophets and thereby superiority over all Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If this hadith equates Ali to the best prophets, do you find yourself resistant to accepting this conclusion? What in your heart makes you hesitate to let Ali be superior to those you already love?
?
The hadith says 'whoever wishes to see... let him look at Ali.' When you look at your own life, whose virtues do you embody? Are you seeking to reflect a prophet, or are you satisfied with less?
?
Razi uses logic to argue for Ali's superiority. Does your attachment to a particular view of the Companions rest on evidence and submission to truth, or on emotion and group loyalty? Would you accept truth even if it meant your preferred companion is not the best?

Classification of Virtues and Ali's Scientific Superiority
Imam Razi classifies virtues and presents the proof of Ali's superior knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's classification of virtues and the proof he offers for Ali's superior knowledge based on a prophetic hadith.

Core Idea
Ali's knowledge was unmatched because the Prophet taught him limitless knowledge.

Imam Razi presents a systematic classification of virtues—spiritual, bodily, and external—and then focuses on spiritual virtues, especially scientific knowledge. He asserts that Ali's knowledge surpassed all other Companions, supported by a hadith where the Prophet mentions teaching Ali a thousand gates of knowledge, each opening a thousand more. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to get the overall meaning.
Notice the structure: classification then proof.
2
Identify the three categories of virtues
Find the three types of virtues mentioned: spiritual, bodily, and external.
The text says 'إما نفسانية وإما بدنية، وإما خارجية'.
3
Understand the subdivision of spiritual virtues
Spiritual virtues are divided into scientific and practical. Note that the proof focuses on the scientific aspect.
This sets up the argument for Ali's knowledge.
4
Analyze the proof for Ali's scientific superiority
The author says he has already proven Ali's knowledge was greater, and strengthens it with a hadith. Examine the hadith: 'a thousand gates, each opening a thousand gates'.
Consider how this serves as evidence.
5
Reflect on the implications
Think about what this proof implies about Ali's status among the Companions.
This is a key point in sectarian discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة العشرون: اعلم أن الفضائل إما نفسانية وإما بدنية، وإما خارجية. أما الفضائل النفسانية فهي مصورة في نوعين: العلمية والعملية. أما العلمية: فقد دللنا على أن علم علي - كرم الله وجهه - كان أكثر من علم سائر الصحابة، ومما يقوي ذلك ما روي قال: علمني رسول الله ألف باب من العلم فانفتح لي من كل باب ألف باب.
The twentieth proof: Know that virtues are either spiritual, or bodily, or external. As for spiritual virtues, they are divided into two types: scientific and practical. As for the scientific: we have already proven that the knowledge of Ali - may Allah honor his face - was more than the knowledge of all other Companions, and among what strengthens that is what was narrated: 'The Messenger of Allah taught me a thousand gates of knowledge, and from each gate a thousand gates opened for me.'
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage presents the twentieth proof for the superiority of Ali ibn Abi Talib. It begins by classifying virtues into three categories: spiritual (nafsāniyya), bodily (badaniyya), and external (khārijiyya). Spiritual virtues are further divided into scientific (ʿilmiyya) and practical (ʿamaliyya). The author then focuses on the scientific virtue: he asserts that Ali's knowledge exceeded that of all other Companions, and supports this with a hadith in which the Prophet claims to have taught Ali a thousand gates of knowledge, each opening a thousand more. This miraculous testimony is presented as conclusive evidence for Ali's intellectual superiority.

Key Terms
فضائل (virtues)
نفسانية (spiritual)
بدنية (bodily)
خارجية (external)
علمية (scientific)
عملية (practical)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith about a thousand gates is merely metaphorical and not to be taken literally.
Correction: Imam Razi presents this hadith as a literal proof for Ali's superior knowledge, indicating it should be understood as factual testimony.

Checkpoint
How does Imam Razi classify virtues in this passage?
A) Into spiritual and bodily only
B) Into spiritual, bodily, and external
C) Into scientific and practical only
D) Into internal and external

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi classifies virtues into three types and uses the hadith of a thousand gates to establish Ali's unparalleled knowledge as a scientific virtue.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that Ali received a thousand gates of knowledge from the Prophet, each opening a thousand more. How many gates of knowledge have you actively sought from the Qur'an and Sunnah today? Name one specific step you will take this week to open a new gate of divine knowledge.
?
The Prophet personally taught Ali because he was qualified and ready. Are you preparing your heart and mind to receive direct guidance from the sources of revelation? What distraction in your life is blocking you from being a true student of prophetic knowledge?
?
Virtues are classified as spiritual, bodily, or external. Look at your own life: are you investing most in external virtues (wealth, appearance) while neglecting the spiritual virtues of knowledge and action? What one change can you make today to prioritize your soul over your image?

Ali's Chastity and Asceticism
Razi presents chastity/asceticism as first virtue, with a claim of discipleship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses Ali's chastity and asceticism to argue for his spiritual superiority, noting that even renowned ascetics among the Companions were his disciples.

Core Idea
Ali's asceticism is the source, not just a peer virtue.

Imam Razi begins his enumeration of Ali's practical virtues with chastity and asceticism. He acknowledges that many Companions were known for these qualities, but asserts that they were all disciples of Ali. This lesson examines that claim and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic snippet and its translation. Notice the names of the ascetics mentioned: Abu Dharr, Salman, Abu al-Darda'.
The phrase 'عليهم السلام [؟]' is unclear in the manuscript but likely refers to Ali.
2
Consider the claim of discipleship
Razi states that these well-known ascetics were 'talamidha' (disciples) of Ali. Reflect on what this implies about Ali's rank in asceticism.
Discipleship suggests a teacher-student relationship, positioning Ali as the source.
3
Connect to the overall argument
This virtue is the first of five cumulative proofs of Ali's superiority over other Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الفضائل النفسانية العملية فأقسام: منها: العفة والزهد وقد كان في الصحابة جمع من الزهاد، كأبي ذر وسلمان وأبي الدرداء، وكلهم كانوا فيه تلامذة عليهم السلام [؟]. ومنها الشجاعة، وقد كان في الصحابة جماعة شجعان كأبي دجانة وخالد بن الوليد وكانت شجاعته أكثر نفعا من شجاعة الكل ألا ترى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال يوم الأحزاب: «الضربة علي خير من عبادة الثقلين» وقال علي بن أبي طالب: والله ما قلعت باب خيبر بقوة جسمانية، لكن بقوة رحمانية. ومنها السخاوة وقد كان في الصحابة جمع من الأسخياء، وقد بلغ إخلاصه في سخاوته إلى أنه أعطى ثلاثة أقراص فأنزل الله تعالى في حقه: وَيُطْعِمُونَ الطَّعَامَ عَلَى حَيْهِ مِسكينا وبتيما وَأَسِيرًا [الإنسان: 8]. ومنها: حسن الخلق، وقد كان مع غاية شجاعته وبسالته حسن الخلق جدا، وقد بلغ فيه إلى حيث ينسبه أعداؤه إلى الدعابة. ومنها البعد عن الدنيا، وظاهر أنه كان مع انفتاح أبواب الدنيا عليه لم يظهر التنعم والتلذذ وكان مع غاية شجاعته إذا شرع في صلاة التهجد وشرع في الدعوات والتضرعات إلى الله تعالى بلغ مبلغاً لا يوازيه أحد ممن جاء بعده من الزهاد، ولما ضربه ابن ملجم قال: «فزت ورب الكعبة».
As for practical spiritual virtues, they are types: among them: chastity and asceticism, and among the Companions were a group of ascetics, like Abu Dharr, Salman, and Abu al-Darda', and all of them were disciples of him – peace be upon them [؟]. And among them: bravery, and among the Companions were a group of brave men like Abu Dujana and Khalid ibn al-Walid, but his bravery was more beneficial than the bravery of all. Do you not see that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said on the Day of the Confederates: 'The strike of Ali is better than the worship of the two heavy ones (humans and jinn)?' And Ali ibn Abi Talib said: 'By Allah, I did not tear down the gate of Khaybar with physical strength, but with divine strength.' And among them: generosity, and among the Companions were a group of generous people, and his sincerity in generosity reached such a degree that he gave three loaves of bread, and Allah the Exalted revealed concerning him: 'And they give food, out of love for Him, to the needy, the orphan, and the captive' [al-Insan: 8]. And among them: good character, and despite his extreme bravery and valor, he was very good-natured, to the extent that his enemies attributed him to jesting. And among them: renunciation of the world, and it is apparent that despite the doors of the world being opened for him, he did not show comfort and pleasure, and despite his extreme bravery, when he engaged in the night prayer (tahajjud) and engaged in supplications and entreaties to Allah the Exalted, he reached a level that no one after him among the ascetics could match. And when Ibn Muljam struck him, he said: 'I have succeeded by the Lord of the Ka'ba.'
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage enumerates five practical spiritual virtues of Ali, each supported by evidence. First, chastity and asceticism: although many Companions were ascetic, they were all disciples of Ali. Second, bravery: Ali's bravery was more beneficial than any other's, as proven by the Prophet's statement at the Battle of the Trench that one strike from Ali surpasses the worship of all humans and jinn, and by Ali's own statement that he took down the gate of Khaybar not by physical strength but by divine power. Third, generosity: Ali gave three loaves of bread, prompting the revelation of Qur'an 76:8. Fourth, good character: despite his bravery, he was so gentle that even his enemies accused him of jesting (i.e., being too lenient). Fifth, renunciation: he shunned worldly pleasures despite having access to them, and his devotion in prayer and supplication was unmatched, culminating in his statement when struck by Ibn Muljam: 'I have succeeded by the Lord of the Ka'ba.' Each virtue is presented as part of the cumulative proof of Ali's superiority over other Companions.

Key Terms
عفة
زهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That many Companions were equally ascetic, so Ali has no distinction.
Correction: Razi argues that despite many ascetics, all were Ali's disciples, establishing his superiority.

Checkpoint
Which three ascetic Companions are named as disciples of Ali?
A) Abu Dharr, Salman, Abu al-Darda'
B) Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman
C) Khalid, Abu Dujana, Ibn Muljam
D) Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, Anas

Key Takeaway
Ali's chastity and asceticism are presented as foundational, with other ascetics learning from him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The companions named were known for their asceticism, yet they considered Ali their teacher. Do you seek knowledge and spirituality from those who are themselves close to the source? Or do you content yourself with second-hand spirituality? What is one step you can take today to connect directly with the original example of Ali?
?
If you claim to follow Ali's path of asceticism, examine your life: is your detachment from worldly desires genuine, or do you still hold on to comforts while admiring the idea? What specific attachment do you need to surrender this week to align with the zuhd of Ali?

Ali's Bravery and Its Divine Source
Razi enumerates bravery with two specific proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two proofs Razi provides for Ali's unmatched bravery: the Prophet's statement at the Battle of the Trench and Ali's own testimony about the gate of Khaybar.

Core Idea
Ali's bravery is divinely aided and surpasses all others.

After asceticism, Razi presents bravery as the second virtue. He compares Ali's bravery to famous warriors like Abu Dujana and Khalid ibn al-Walid, then provides two pieces of evidence that elevate Ali above them: a Prophetic hadith and Ali's own statement about divine strength. This lesson examines those proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two pieces of evidence: the hadith from the Battle of the Trench and Ali's statement about the gate of Khaybar.
2
Analyze the Prophetic hadith
The Prophet said: 'The strike of Ali is better than the worship of the two heavy ones (thaqalayn).' Reflect on the magnitude of this statement.
Thaqalayn refers to humans and jinn.
3
Examine Ali's own testimony
Ali said he did not take down the gate of Khaybar with physical strength but with divine strength. What does this say about the nature of his bravery?
This emphasizes the spiritual dimension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الفضائل النفسانية العملية فأقسام: منها: العفة والزهد وقد كان في الصحابة جمع من الزهاد، كأبي ذر وسلمان وأبي الدرداء، وكلهم كانوا فيه تلامذة عليهم السلام [؟]. ومنها الشجاعة، وقد كان في الصحابة جماعة شجعان كأبي دجانة وخالد بن الوليد وكانت شجاعته أكثر نفعا من شجاعة الكل ألا ترى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال يوم الأحزاب: «الضربة علي خير من عبادة الثقلين» وقال علي بن أبي طالب: والله ما قلعت باب خيبر بقوة جسمانية، لكن بقوة رحمانية. ومنها السخاوة وقد كان في الصحابة جمع من الأسخياء، وقد بلغ إخلاصه في سخاوته إلى أنه أعطى ثلاثة أقراص فأنزل الله تعالى في حقه: وَيُطْعِمُونَ الطَّعَامَ عَلَى حَيْهِ مِسكينا وبتيما وَأَسِيرًا [الإنسان: 8]. ومنها: حسن الخلق، وقد كان مع غاية شجاعته وبسالته حسن الخلق جدا، وقد بلغ فيه إلى حيث ينسبه أعداؤه إلى الدعابة. ومنها البعد عن الدنيا، وظاهر أنه كان مع انفتاح أبواب الدنيا عليه لم يظهر التنعم والتلذذ وكان مع غاية شجاعته إذا شرع في صلاة التهجد وشرع في الدعوات والتضرعات إلى الله تعالى بلغ مبلغاً لا يوازيه أحد ممن جاء بعده من الزهاد، ولما ضربه ابن ملجم قال: «فزت ورب الكعبة».
As for practical spiritual virtues, they are types: among them: chastity and asceticism, and among the Companions were a group of ascetics, like Abu Dharr, Salman, and Abu al-Darda', and all of them were disciples of him – peace be upon them [؟]. And among them: bravery, and among the Companions were a group of brave men like Abu Dujana and Khalid ibn al-Walid, but his bravery was more beneficial than the bravery of all. Do you not see that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said on the Day of the Confederates: 'The strike of Ali is better than the worship of the two heavy ones (humans and jinn)?' And Ali ibn Abi Talib said: 'By Allah, I did not tear down the gate of Khaybar with physical strength, but with divine strength.' And among them: generosity, and among the Companions were a group of generous people, and his sincerity in generosity reached such a degree that he gave three loaves of bread, and Allah the Exalted revealed concerning him: 'And they give food, out of love for Him, to the needy, the orphan, and the captive' [al-Insan: 8]. And among them: good character, and despite his extreme bravery and valor, he was very good-natured, to the extent that his enemies attributed him to jesting. And among them: renunciation of the world, and it is apparent that despite the doors of the world being opened for him, he did not show comfort and pleasure, and despite his extreme bravery, when he engaged in the night prayer (tahajjud) and engaged in supplications and entreaties to Allah the Exalted, he reached a level that no one after him among the ascetics could match. And when Ibn Muljam struck him, he said: 'I have succeeded by the Lord of the Ka'ba.'
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage enumerates five practical spiritual virtues of Ali, each supported by evidence. First, chastity and asceticism: although many Companions were ascetic, they were all disciples of Ali. Second, bravery: Ali's bravery was more beneficial than any other's, as proven by the Prophet's statement at the Battle of the Trench that one strike from Ali surpasses the worship of all humans and jinn, and by Ali's own statement that he took down the gate of Khaybar not by physical strength but by divine power. Third, generosity: Ali gave three loaves of bread, prompting the revelation of Qur'an 76:8. Fourth, good character: despite his bravery, he was so gentle that even his enemies accused him of jesting (i.e., being too lenient). Fifth, renunciation: he shunned worldly pleasures despite having access to them, and his devotion in prayer and supplication was unmatched, culminating in his statement when struck by Ibn Muljam: 'I have succeeded by the Lord of the Ka'ba.' Each virtue is presented as part of the cumulative proof of Ali's superiority over other Companions.

شجاعة
ضربة
باب خيبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali's bravery was purely physical like other warriors.
Correction: Razi shows his bravery had a divine source and was spiritually supreme.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say about Ali's strike on the Day of the Confederates?
A) It is better than the worship of all humans and jinn.
B) It is equal to the worship of all prophets.
C) It is the greatest military feat.
D) It is a sign of physical strength.

Key Takeaway
Ali's bravery is not merely physical but divinely empowered, making it superior to all others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Ali’s single strike is better than the worship of all jinn and humans, what does that reveal about the value of your own worship? Do you rely on your own efforts or on divine aid to make your deeds weighty?
?
Ali admitted that his strength was not physical but divine. When you accomplish something good, do you truly attribute it to Allah's help, or do you silently credit your own ability? Which belief is more present in your heart?
?
The Prophet raised one act of Ali above all worship of creation. This demands you examine the quality, not just quantity, of your deeds. Are you content with routine worship, or are you striving for actions that are infused with divine strength and sincerity?

Ali's Generosity and the Qur'anic Witness
Razi cites the revelation of al-Insan 8 as proof of Ali's generosity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the revelation of Qur'an 76:8 to prove the superior quality of Ali's generosity.

Core Idea
Ali's generosity was so profound that it prompted Qur'anic revelation.

The third virtue is generosity. Razi states that Ali's sincerity in giving reached such a level that when he gave three loaves of bread to a needy, orphan, and captive, Allah revealed a verse in the Qur'an about feeding others. This lesson focuses on that verse as a divine endorsement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the specific act: giving three loaves of bread to three categories of recipients.
The verse is from Surah al-Insan (76:8).
2
Connect the act to the revelation
Razi claims that this act was the cause (sabab) for the revelation of the verse. Reflect on what this means for Ali's status.
The verse praises those who feed others 'out of love for Him'.
3
Consider the uniqueness
While many companions were generous, only Ali's generosity is directly tied to a revealed verse.

?

Ali's Good Character Amidst Bravery
Razi presents good character as a virtue of Ali, noting his mildness despite valor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi describes Ali's good character as complementary to his bravery, even to the point of being accused of jesting by enemies.

Core Idea
Ali's gentleness, even in strength, confounded his opponents.

The fourth virtue is good character. Razi notes that despite Ali's extreme bravery and valor, he was very good-natured, so much so that his enemies attributed his kindness to jesting. This lesson explores that balance.

Guided Path
1
Read the short passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Observe the contrast between 'shaja'ah' (bravery) and 'husn al-khuluq' (good character).
2
Understand the accusation
The enemies described Ali as having 'duba'ah' (jesting/playfulness). Why would they say that?
This likely stemmed from his gentle demeanor, which they misinterpreted as levity.

?

?

?

What does that reveal about the consistency of your character? Ask Allah to grant you the balance of shajāʿah and ḥilm as seen in Ali.

Ali's Renunciation and Devotional Supremacy
Razi concludes the virtues with renunciation, providing evidence from Ali's behavior and his final words.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi proves Ali's renunciation by highlighting his detachment from worldly pleasures despite access, and his unparalleled devotion in night prayers and supplications.

Core Idea
Ali turned away from the world even when it was at his feet.

The final virtue is renunciation of the world. Razi points out that even though the doors of the world were open to Ali, he did not indulge in comfort. Moreover, his night prayers and supplications were unmatched. The ultimate proof is his statement when struck by his assassin: 'I have succeeded by the Lord of the Ka'ba.' This lesson examines these proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two aspects: not showing comfort/pleasure, and his devotion in tahajjud and supplication.
2
Reflect on his detachment
Despite being in a position of power and wealth, Ali did not indulge in worldly pleasures. What does this say about his priorities?
True renunciation is not lack of wealth but detachment.
3
Consider his final words
When struck by Ibn Muljam, Ali said 'Fuztu wa rabbi al-ka'bah' (I have succeeded by the Lord of the Ka'ba). What does this reveal about his state of mind?
He rejoiced at martyrdom as the ultimate triumph.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الفضائل النفسانية العملية فأقسام: منها: العفة والزهد وقد كان في الصحابة جمع من الزهاد، كأبي ذر وسلمان وأبي الدرداء، وكلهم كانوا فيه تلامذة عليهم السلام [؟]. ومنها الشجاعة، وقد كان في الصحابة جماعة شجعان كأبي دجانة وخالد بن الوليد وكانت شجاعته أكثر نفعا من شجاعة الكل ألا ترى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال يوم الأحزاب: «الضربة علي خير من عبادة الثقلين» وقال علي بن أبي طالب: والله ما قلعت باب خيبر بقوة جسمانية، لكن بقوة رحمانية. ومنها السخاوة وقد كان في الصحابة جمع من الأسخياء، وقد بلغ إخلاصه في سخاوته إلى أنه أعطى ثلاثة أقراص فأنزل الله تعالى في حقه: وَيُطْعِمُونَ الطَّعَامَ عَلَى حَيْهِ مِسكينا وبتيما وَأَسِيرًا [الإنسان: 8]. ومنها: حسن الخلق، وقد كان مع غاية شجاعته وبسالته حسن الخلق جدا، وقد بلغ فيه إلى حيث ينسبه أعداؤه إلى الدعابة. ومنها البعد عن الدنيا، وظاهر أنه كان مع انفتاح أبواب الدنيا عليه لم يظهر التنعم والتلذذ وكان مع غاية شجاعته إذا شرع في صلاة التهجد وشرع في الدعوات والتضرعات إلى الله تعالى بلغ مبلغاً لا يوازيه أحد ممن جاء بعده من الزهاد، ولما ضربه ابن ملجم قال: «فزت ورب الكعبة».
As for practical spiritual virtues, they are types: among them: chastity and asceticism, and among the Companions were a group of ascetics, like Abu Dharr, Salman, and Abu al-Darda', and all of them were disciples of him – peace be upon them [؟]. And among them: bravery, and among the Companions were a group of brave men like Abu Dujana and Khalid ibn al-Walid, but his bravery was more beneficial than the bravery of all. Do you not see that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said on the Day of the Confederates: 'The strike of Ali is better than the worship of the two heavy ones (humans and jinn)?' And Ali ibn Abi Talib said: 'By Allah, I did not tear down the gate of Khaybar with physical strength, but with divine strength.' And among them: generosity, and among the Companions were a group of generous people, and his sincerity in generosity reached such a degree that he gave three loaves of bread, and Allah the Exalted revealed concerning him: 'And they give food, out of love for Him, to the needy, the orphan, and the captive' [al-Insan: 8]. And among them: good character, and despite his extreme bravery and valor, he was very good-natured, to the extent that his enemies attributed him to jesting. And among them: renunciation of the world, and it is apparent that despite the doors of the world being opened for him, he did not show comfort and pleasure, and despite his extreme bravery, when he engaged in the night prayer (tahajjud) and engaged in supplications and entreaties to Allah the Exalted, he reached a level that no one after him among the ascetics could match. And when Ibn Muljam struck him, he said: 'I have succeeded by the Lord of the Ka'ba.'
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage enumerates five practical spiritual virtues of Ali, each supported by evidence. First, chastity and asceticism: although many Companions were ascetic, they were all disciples of Ali. Second, bravery: Ali's bravery was more beneficial than any other's, as proven by the Prophet's statement at the Battle of the Trench that one strike from Ali surpasses the worship of all humans and jinn, and by Ali's own statement that he took down the gate of Khaybar not by physical strength but by divine power. Third, generosity: Ali gave three loaves of bread, prompting the revelation of Qur'an 76:8. Fourth, good character: despite his bravery, he was so gentle that even his enemies accused him of jesting (i.e., being too lenient). Fifth, renunciation: he shunned worldly pleasures despite having access to them, and his devotion in prayer and supplication was unmatched, culminating in his statement when struck by Ibn Muljam: 'I have succeeded by the Lord of the Ka'ba.' Each virtue is presented as part of the cumulative proof of Ali's superiority over other Companions.

Key Terms
بعد عن الدنيا
تهجد
تضرعات
فزت ورب الكعبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Renunciation means poverty; Ali was rich but renounced enjoyment.
Correction: True renunciation is detachment from worldly pleasures, not lack of wealth.

Checkpoint
What did Ali say when struck by Ibn Muljam?
A) 'I have succeeded by the Lord of the Ka'ba.'
B) 'I am patient with Allah's decree.'
C) 'Woe to the son of the Jew.'
D) 'This is the path of truth.'

Key Takeaway
Ali's renunciation was demonstrated by his detachment from material pleasures and his supreme devotion in worship, culminating in his joyous martyrdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ali had the world at his feet yet rejected comfort. What worldly comfort are you clinging to that holds you back from true devotion? What would it cost you to let it go today?
?
When struck by the assassin's blade, Ali's first words were 'I have succeeded.' If your life ended right now, would you have the same confidence? What needs to change so that your last words could echo his?
?
Ali's unparalleled bravery did not prevent him from weeping in prayer at night. What excuse do you use to avoid deepening your prayer life? Is your courage reserved only for worldly pursuits?

Ali's Physical Strength
Brief mention of Ali's strength as the first bodily virtue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi presents Ali's physical strength as evidence of his superiority.

Core Idea
Ali's strength was so great he could sever necks like cutting pens.

Imam Razi begins his argument for Ali's bodily virtues with the most tangible one: physical strength. This short but vivid passage uses a striking simile to emphasize Ali's prowess, showing that his excellence was not only spiritual but also manifest in his body.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on strength
Read the Arabic sentence carefully. Notice how it begins with 'فمنها' to introduce the first virtue. The simile 'قطع الأقلام' is meant to show ease and precision.
2
Understand the claim
The claim is that Ali possessed great strength and severity. The evidence is an anecdotal saying that he used to cut necks as if cutting pens. This is meant to illustrate his physical dominance.
Severity here refers to his firmness in battle.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Why does Razi begin with a bodily virtue? Consider that the whole passage is about external virtues that are easy to observe. Strength is a clear, undeniable sign of superiority.
This strength is not just physical but also a metaphor for his spiritual strength.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الفضائل البدنية: فمنها: القوة والشدة: وكان فيهما عظيم الدرجة حتى قيل: إنه كان يقطع الهام قطع الأقلام. ومنها النسب العالي ومعلوم أن أشرف الأنساب هو القرب من رسول الله، وهو كان أقرب الناس في النسب إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأما العباس، فإنه وإن كان عم رسول الله إلا أن العباس كان أخا لعبد الله والد رسول الله من الأب لا من الأم، وأما أبو طالب فإنه كان أخا لعبد الله والد رسول الله من الأب والأم. وأيضًا فإن عليا كان هاشميًا من الأب والأم؛ لأنه علي بن أبي طالب بن عبد المطلب بن هاشم وأيضًا أم علي بن أبي طالب فاطمة أسد بنت بن هاشم. ومنها المصاهرة ولم يكن لأحد من الخلق مصاهرة مثل ما كانت له. وأما عثمان فهو وإن شركه في كونه صهرا للرسول إلا أن أشرف أولاد الرسول هو فاطمة، ولذلك قال: سيدة نساء العالمين أربع وعدها منهن. ولم يحصل مثل هذا الشرف للبنتين اللتين هما زوجتا عثمان. ومنها: أنه لم يكن لأحد من الصحابة أولاد يشاركون أولاده في الفضيلة كالحسن والحسين، وهما سيدا شباب أهل الجنة - ولداه. ثم انظر إلى أولاد الحسن مثل الحسن المثنى والمثلث وعبد الله المثنى، والنفس الزكية وإلى أولاد الحسين مثل زين العابدين، والباقر والصادق، والكاظم، والرضا، فإن هؤلاء الأكابر يقر بفضيلتهم وعلو درجتهم كل مسلم. ومما يدل على علو شأنهم أن أفضل المشايخ وأعلاهم درجة هو أبو يزيد البسطامي، وكان نشأ في دار جعفر الصادق، وأما معروف الكرخي فإنه أسلم على يد علي بن موسى الرضا، وكان بواب داره وبقي على هذه الحالة إلى آخر عمره، ومعلوم أن أمثال هذه الأولاد لم يتفق لأحد من الصحابة. ولو أخذنا في الشرح والإطناب لطال الكلام. فهذا مجموع دلائل من قال بتفضيل أمير المؤمنين علي بن أبي طالب.
As for bodily virtues: among them: strength and severity: he was of great degree in both, so that it was said: he used to cut necks as if cutting pens. And among them: high lineage. It is known that the most honorable of lineages is closeness to the Messenger of Allah, and he was the closest of people in lineage to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. As for al-‘Abbas, although he was the uncle of the Messenger of Allah, al-‘Abbas was the brother of ‘Abdullah, the father of the Messenger of Allah, from the father (only) not from the mother. And as for Abu Talib, he was the brother of ‘Abdullah, the father of the Messenger of Allah, from both father and mother. Also, ‘Ali was a Hashimite from both father and mother, because he is ‘Ali ibn Abi Talib ibn ‘Abd al-Muttalib ibn Hashim, and also the mother of ‘Ali ibn Abi Talib, Fatima bint Asad, was from the family of Hashim. And among them: marital relation (musahara). No one among creation had a marital relation like his. As for ‘Uthman, although he shared with him in being a son-in-law of the Messenger, the most honorable of the children of the Messenger is Fatima, and therefore he said: 'The mistress of the women of the worlds is four' and he counted her among them. And such honor was not attained by the two daughters who were the wives of ‘Uthman. And among them: that no one among the Companions had children who shared in virtue with his children like al-Hasan and al-Husayn, who are the masters of the youth of Paradise – his two sons. Then look at the children of al-Hasan, such as al-Hasan al-Muthanna and al-Muthallath and ‘Abdullah al-Muthanna and al-Nafs al-Zakiyya, and at the children of al-Husayn, such as Zayn al-‘Abidin, al-Baqir, al-Sadiq, al-Kazim, and al-Rida. For these great ones, every Muslim acknowledges their virtue and high station. Among the proofs of their high station is that the best of the shaykhs and the highest in degree is Abu Yazid al-Bistami, and he was raised in the house of Ja‘far al-Sadiq. As for Ma‘ruf al-Karkhi, he accepted Islam at the hand of ‘Ali ibn Musa al-Rida, and was the doorkeeper of his house and remained in that condition until the end of his life. And it is known that such children were not granted to any of the Companions. And if we were to elaborate and expound, the speech would become lengthy. This is the totality of evidence from those who said that the Commander of the Faithful ‘Ali ibn Abi Talib is superior.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage presents the bodily virtues of Ali, beginning with physical strength, evidenced by a saying that he could sever necks like cutting pens. Next is his noble lineage: he is the closest relative to the Prophet in terms of genealogy, being a Hashimite from both parents. His father Abu Talib was the full brother of the Prophet's father, while his mother Fatima bint Asad was also Hashimite. Third, his marital relation (musahara) by marrying Fatima, the Prophet's most honored daughter, who is the mistress of women. Even 'Uthman's marriage to two daughters of the Prophet does not match this honor. Fourth, his children: Hasan and Husayn are the masters of the youth of Paradise, and their descendants include the Imams (Zayn al-'Abidin, al-Baqir, al-Sadiq, al-Kazim, al-Rida) who are universally recognized as virtuous. The author further demonstrates the spiritual stature of these descendants by noting that the great Sufi Abu Yazid al-Bistami was raised in the house of Ja'far al-Sadiq, and Ma'ruf al-Karkhi converted at the hands of and served Imam al-Rida. The passage concludes that no other Companion had such virtuous children, and that this completes the proofs for Ali's superiority.

Key Terms
قوة
شدة
هام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What simile is used to describe Ali's strength?
A) Like a lion tearing prey
B) Cutting necks like cutting pens
C) Breaking iron bars like sticks
D) Uprooting trees like weeds

Key Takeaway
Ali's physical strength was so extraordinary that it was likened to the effortless cutting of pens.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ali's physical strength is highlighted as a bodily virtue. What physical or bodily blessings has Allah given you? How are you using them in His service, and are there areas where you need to realign your priorities?
?
The author describes Ali's strength as 'cutting necks like pens'—a display of power in battle. If you are not in a position of physical combat, what are the 'battles' you face in your life where you need to embody strength? Will you commit to being strong in upholding truth, even when it costs you?
?
This lesson treats bodily strength as a praiseworthy trait. In a culture that often values appearance over substance, how does this shift your understanding of what it means to be virtuous? Are you cultivating strength in your character and body for the sake of Allah, or are you neglecting this aspect of your faith?

Ali's Noble Lineage
Detailed argument for Ali's noble lineage through both parents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi proves that Ali's lineage from both parents makes him the closest relative to the Prophet.

Core Idea
Ali is a Hashimite from both father and mother, unmatched in lineage.

Imam Razi now turns to Ali's lineage, a central virtue in Islamic honor. He compares Ali's genealogy to that of other relatives, showing that Ali is uniquely close to the Prophet through both his father and mother, both being from the Banu Hashim clan.

Guided Path
1
Read the lineage passage
Read from 'ومنها النسب العالي' to 'بنت بن هاشم'. Notice the comparisons with al-‘Abbas and Abu Talib.
2
Compare with other relatives
The author explains that al-‘Abbas is only a paternal half-uncle, while Abu Talib is a full uncle. But Ali is not only a Hashimite through his father but also his mother Fatima bint Asad was Hashimite.
This makes Ali a Hashimite on both sides, a rare distinction.
3
Recognize the argument's strength
The point is that closeness to the Prophet in lineage is best measured by being a Hashimite from both parents. No other Companion had this double Hashimite lineage.
The Prophet himself was a Hashimite; Ali shares that exact ancestry.

Source Text

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that al-‘Abbas or Abu Talib had a closer lineage because they are uncles.
Correction: The author shows that being a Hashimite from both parents is superior. Ali's mother was also Hashimite, which no other Companion had.

Checkpoint
How does Imam Razi prove that Ali's lineage is doubly noble?
A) Because his father was the Prophet's cousin
B) Because both his father and mother were from the Banu Hashim clan
C) Because he was adopted by the Prophet
D) Because his grandfather was Abd al-Muttalib

Key Takeaway
Ali's lineage is uniquely noble because he is a Hashimite from both parents, making him the closest relative to the Prophet in genealogy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your family lineage were like Ali's—noble on both sides—would you feel spiritually superior? Or does this passage remind you that true honor is from taqwa alone? How can you ensure you don't pride yourself on ancestry?
?
Ali's mother was also from the noble lineage of Hashim. Have you ever undervalued your mother's family in your identity? How can you honor both sides of your lineage as Ali's legacy does?
?
The Prophet said the most honorable is the most righteous. Yet this passage emphasizes Ali's physical closeness to the Prophet. How do you reconcile these two? Could it be that Ali's righteousness is linked to his lineage? What does your own life say about the connection between heritage and character?

Ali's Marital Relation with the Prophet
Comparison of Ali's marital relation with the Prophet versus that of ‘Uthman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Razi considers Ali's marriage to Fatima as a unique honor unmatched by any other Companion.

Core Idea
No one had a marital relation like Ali's marriage to Fatima, the mistress of women.

Imam Razi now presents the third bodily virtue: the marital relation (musahara) with the Prophet. He argues that although ‘Uthman also married two daughters of the Prophet, Ali's wife Fatima holds a special station as the most honored daughter, making Ali's connection superior.

Guided Path
1
Read the musahara passage
Read from 'ومنها المصاهرة' to 'البنتين اللتين هما زوجتا عثمان'. Note the comparison with ‘Uthman.
2
Understand the superiority of Fatima
The author points out that Fatima is the most honored daughter of the Prophet, calling her one of the four mistresses of women. This honor is not shared by the other daughters married to ‘Uthman.
The hadith of the four mistresses is referenced, though not quoted fully.
3
Reflect on the unique honor
Ali's marital tie is unique because it is with the best of the Prophet's children. No other Companion had that privilege.
This strengthens the argument for Ali's superiority.

وأما الفضائل البدنية: فمنها: القوة والشدة: وكان فيهما عظيم الدرجة حتى قيل: إنه كان يقطع الهام قطع الأقلام. ومنها النسب العالي ومعلوم أن أشرف الأنساب هو القرب من رسول الله، وهو كان أقرب الناس في النسب إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأما العباس، فإنه وإن كان عم رسول الله إلا أن العباس كان أخا لعبد الله والد رسول الله من الأب لا من الأم، وأما أبو طالب فإنه كان أخا لعبد الله والد رسول الله من الأب والأم. وأيضًا فإن عليا كان هاشميًا من الأب والأم؛ لأنه علي بن أبي طالب بن عبد المطلب بن هاشم وأيضًا أم علي بن أبي طالب فاطمة أسد بنت بن هاشم. ومنها المصاهرة ولم يكن لأحد من الخلق مصاهرة مثل ما كانت له. وأما عثمان فهو وإن شركه في كونه صهرا للرسول إلا أن أشرف أولاد الرسول هو فاطمة، ولذلك قال: سيدة نساء العالمين أربع وعدها منهن. ولم يحصل مثل هذا الشرف للبنتين اللتين هما زوجتا عثمان. ومنها: أنه لم يكن لأحد من الصحابة أولاد يشاركون أولاده في الفضيلة كالحسن والحسين، وهما سيدا شباب أهل الجنة - ولداه. ثم انظر إلى أولاد الحسن مثل الحسن المثنى والمثلث وعبد الله المثنى، والنفس الزكية وإلى أولاد الحسين مثل زين العابدين، والباقر والصادق، والكاظم، والرضا، فإن هؤلاء الأكابر يقر بفضيلتهم وعلو درجتهم كل مسلم. ومما يدل على علو شأنهم أن أفضل المشايخ وأعلاهم درجة هو أبو يزيد البسطامي، وكان نشأ في دار جعفر الصادق، وأما معروف الكرخي فإنه أسلم على يد علي بن موسى الرضا، وكان بواب داره وبقي على هذه الحالة إلى آخر عمره، ومعلوم أن أمثال هذه الأولاد لم يتفق لأحد من الصحابة. ولو أخذنا في الشرح والإطناب لطال الكلام. فهذا مجموع دلائل من قال بتفضيل أمير المؤمنين علي بن أبي طالب.
As for bodily virtues: among them: strength and severity: he was of great degree in both, so that it was said: he used to cut necks as if cutting pens. And among them: high lineage. It is known that the most honorable of lineages is closeness to the Messenger of Allah, and he was the closest of people in lineage to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. As for al-‘Abbas, although he was the uncle of the Messenger of Allah, al-‘Abbas was the brother of ‘Abdullah, the father of the Messenger of Allah, from the father (only) not from the mother. And as for Abu Talib, he was the brother of ‘Abdullah, the father of the Messenger of Allah, from both father and mother. Also, ‘Ali was a Hashimite from both father and mother, because he is ‘Ali ibn Abi Talib ibn ‘Abd al-Muttalib ibn Hashim, and also the mother of ‘Ali ibn Abi Talib, Fatima bint Asad, was from the family of Hashim. And among them: marital relation (musahara). No one among creation had a marital relation like his. As for ‘Uthman, although he shared with him in being a son-in-law of the Messenger, the most honorable of the children of the Messenger is Fatima, and therefore he said: 'The mistress of the women of the worlds is four' and he counted her among them. And such honor was not attained by the two daughters who were the wives of ‘Uthman. And among them: that no one among the Companions had children who shared in virtue with his children like al-Hasan and al-Husayn, who are the masters of the youth of Paradise – his two sons. Then look at the children of al-Hasan, such as al-Hasan al-Muthanna and al-Muthallath and ‘Abdullah al-Muthanna and al-Nafs al-Zakiyya, and at the children of al-Husayn, such as Zayn al-‘Abidin, al-Baqir, al-Sadiq, al-Kazim, and al-Rida. For these great ones, every Muslim acknowledges their virtue and high station. Among the proofs of their high station is that the best of the shaykhs and the highest in degree is Abu Yazid al-Bistami, and he was raised in the house of Ja‘far al-Sadiq. As for Ma‘ruf al-Karkhi, he accepted Islam at the hand of ‘Ali ibn Musa al-Rida, and was the doorkeeper of his house and remained in that condition until the end of his life. And it is known that such children were not granted to any of the Companions. And if we were to elaborate and expound, the speech would become lengthy. This is the totality of evidence from those who said that the Commander of the Faithful ‘Ali ibn Abi Talib is superior.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage presents the bodily virtues of Ali, beginning with physical strength, evidenced by a saying that he could sever necks like cutting pens. Next is his noble lineage: he is the closest relative to the Prophet in terms of genealogy, being a Hashimite from both parents. His father Abu Talib was the full brother of the Prophet's father, while his mother Fatima bint Asad was also Hashimite. Third, his marital relation (musahara) by marrying Fatima, the Prophet's most honored daughter, who is the mistress of women. Even 'Uthman's marriage to two daughters of the Prophet does not match this honor. Fourth, his children: Hasan and Husayn are the masters of the youth of Paradise, and their descendants include the Imams (Zayn al-'Abidin, al-Baqir, al-Sadiq, al-Kazim, al-Rida) who are universally recognized as virtuous. The author further demonstrates the spiritual stature of these descendants by noting that the great Sufi Abu Yazid al-Bistami was raised in the house of Ja'far al-Sadiq, and Ma'ruf al-Karkhi converted at the hands of and served Imam al-Rida. The passage concludes that no other Companion had such virtuous children, and that this completes the proofs for Ali's superiority.

Key Terms
مصاهرة
صهر
فاطمة
سيدة النساء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does Imam Razi counter the argument that ‘Uthman also had a marital relation with the Prophet?
A) By saying ‘Uthman was not a true Companion
B) By stating that Fatima is the most honored daughter of the Prophet
C) By denying that ‘Uthman married the Prophet's daughters
D) By claiming that ‘Uthman's marriage was not legitimate

Key Takeaway
Ali's marital relation with the Prophet is unique because he married Fatima, the most honored daughter and mistress of women.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever measure your worth by the status of your family or spouse, rather than by your own spiritual standing? How would you feel if you were compared to someone like Ali, whose honor came from his wife's virtue?
?
What is the 'Fatima' in your life—the person or relationship that could elevate you if you honored them purely for their closeness to Allah? Are you investing in that relationship?
?
If you were to lose all your worldly connections except your relationship with the Prophet's family, would you still consider yourself honored? What steps can you take today to strengthen that connection?

Ali's Virtuous Children and Descendants
Enumeration of Ali's children and descendants with proofs of their high spiritual status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the virtue of Ali's children and descendants, including the Imams and their spiritual impact, demonstrates his superiority.

Core Idea
Ali's children al-Hasan and al-Husayn are masters of Paradise's youth, and their descendants include great Imams and saints.

Imam Razi presents the fourth and final bodily virtue: the excellence of Ali's offspring. He specifically mentions al-Hasan and al-Husayn, then expands to their descendants, including the Imams. He provides examples of great Sufi saints who were connected to these descendants, showing their spiritual influence reaches even outside the Shia tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the children passage
Read from 'ومنها: أنه لم يكن لأحد' to 'فهذا مجموع دلائل'. Notice the list of descendants and the stories of Abu Yazid and Ma‘ruf.
2
Identify the key descendants
The passage names al-Hasan and al-Husayn as masters of Paradise's youth. Then it lists their descendants: from al-Hasan: al-Muthanna, al-Muthallath, ‘Abdullah al-Muthanna, al-Nafs al-Zakiyya; from al-Husayn: Zayn al-‘Abidin, al-Baqir, al-Sadiq, al-Kazim, al-Rida.
These are recognized as great scholars and Imams.
3
Understand the spiritual proof
The author gives two examples: Abu Yazid al-Bistami, the great Sufi saint, was raised in the house of Ja‘far al-Sadiq, and Ma‘ruf al-Karkhi converted at the hand of Imam al-Rida and served him. This shows the spiritual station of these descendants.
This is a powerful argument from effect: such great saints were products of the lineage.
4
Connect to the overall argument
The author concludes that no other Companion had children of such virtue, and this completes the proofs for Ali's superiority.
The phrase 'فهذا مجموع دلائل من قال بتفضيل' summarizes the whole section.

?

Commit to one concrete step this week to connect with authentic spiritual guides.
?

?
